<h2 scrollto-destination=192156920 id=\"192156920\" class=\"abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present new observations of two <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span>\u00a0=\u00a00.12 strong-lensing elliptical galaxies, originally discovered from the SDSS-IV MaNGA survey, using the new FOCAS IFU spectrograph on the Subaru Telescope. For J1436+4943, our observations confirm the identification of this system as a multiple-image lens, in a cusp configuration, with an Einstein radius \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.0\u2009arcsec. For J1701+3722, the improved data confirm earlier hints of a complex source plane, with different configurations evident in different emission lines. The new observations reveal a previously unseen inner counter-image to the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] arc found from MaNGA, leading to a smaller revised Einstein radius of \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.6\u2009arcsec. The inferred projected masses within the Einstein apertures (3.7\u20134.7\u2009kpc) are consistent with being dominated by stars with an initial mass function (IMF) similar to that of the Milky Way, and a dark matter contribution of \u223c35\u00a0per\u2009cent as supported from cosmological simulations. These results are consistent with \u2018pure lensing\u2019 analyses of lower redshift lenses, but contrast with claims for heavier IMFs from combined lensing and dynamical studies of more distant early-type galaxies.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD&quot;\">galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156922 id=\"192156922\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Strong gravitational lensing is a key tool for measuring extragalactic masses and probing the distribution of dark and luminous matter in galaxies (e.g. Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). Analysing a sample of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00.2 strong-lensing elliptical galaxies, Treu et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) found that their velocity dispersions and projected lensing masses could only be reconciled with a universal dark matter profile if the stellar mass-to-light ratio, <em>\u03a5</em>, was larger than expected for an initial mass function (IMF) like that in the Milky Way (e.g. Kroupa <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). By contrast, for the few known nearby (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$z$|</span>\u00a0=\u00a00.03\u20130.07) strong lenses, lensing <em>alone</em> constrains <em>\u03a5</em> to be close to the value expected from the Kroupa IMF (Collier, Smith\u00a0&amp; Lucey <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). In these low-redshift systems, the arcs are formed at smaller physical radius, minimizing the contributions from dark matter, which obviates the need for dynamical information to separate dark and stellar components. One possible resolution of the tension between the above results, discussed by Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), is that steep inner gradients in <em>\u03a5</em> may inflate the central velocity dispersion, causing the combined lensing and dynamics analysis to assign too much mass to the stellar component and too little to the dark halo.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Establishing well-constrained lenses at intermediate distances should help to solve the apparent discrepancy between the nearby and distant samples. Smith, Lucey\u00a0&amp; Conroy (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) presented the first use of integral field unit (IFU) spectroscopy as a tool to discover lensed line-emitting sources behind bright foreground galaxies. This method, applied to individually targeted lens candidates, has also been adapted to the VLT MUSE spectrograph (Smith et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Collier et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1_68_1579329418409\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1_68_1579329418409\" data-open=\"bib1_68_1579329418409\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>). A complementary approach is to exploit data from large multi-IFU surveys. The SDSS-IV MaNGA survey (Bundy et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) is acquiring IFU observations for thousands of nearby galaxies, including hundreds of massive ellipticals, which are the most effective gravitational lenses.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Two groups have searched the MaNGA data cubes for lens systems. Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) (and unpublished extensions) conducted a semi-automated search in the MaNGA data releases DR13\u2013DR15, restricted to \u223c600 galaxies with a velocity dispersion \u03c3\u00a0&gt;\u00a0200\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>, which dominate the total strong-lensing cross-section. Independently, Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) searched all targets in DR13\u2013DR14 using a more automated source detection method, though retaining a manual inspection step. Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) reported the discovery of a lensed source behind J1701+3722, apparently showing a near-complete Einstein ring in [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], but only a single \u2018arc\u2019 in [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]. He estimated an Einstein radius of 2.3\u2009arcsec, but noted that this is uncomfortably large compared to the measured velocity dispersion. The Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) search yielded seven new apparent multiple-imaging systems as well as confirming the identification of J1701+3722. In a subsequent reanalysis of the data, we could not convincingly reproduce many of these systems (see discussion in Smith, Lucey\u00a0&amp; Collier <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), but J1436+4943, which was missed in Smith\u2019s visual search, is a compelling candidate for further study.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this letter, we present follow-up observations of J1436+4943 and J1701+3722, obtained with the new IFU mode of the FOCAS spectrograph at the Subaru telescope (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>). The new observations have much higher spatial resolution than the MaNGA discovery data, and also higher spectral resolution, enabling a more detailed reanalysis of the two lenses (Sections\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>). Combining the measured Einstein radii with photometry and estimates for the dark matter contributions and likely stellar ages, we derive results on the total and stellar mass-to-light ratios, and constraints on the IMF through the mass-excess factor (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>). The work is briefly summarized in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We adopt the cosmological parameters from Planck Collaboration VI (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156928 id=\"192156928\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 SUBARU FOCAS IFU OBSERVATIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We observed J1436+4943 and J1701+3722 using the Subaru FOCAS IFU during its first night of scientific operations, on 2019 June 26. The design and characteristics of the IFU are fully described by Ozaki et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, and in preparation). Briefly, the unit is an image slicer that reformats a 10.1\u00a0\u00d7\u00a013.5\u2009arcsec<sup>2</sup> field of view into 23 slices of width 0.44\u2009arcsec, sampled with 0.2\u2009arcsec pixels; the IFU feeds the existing FOCAS spectrograph (Kashikawa et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). We observed with the VPH900 grism, providing a wavelength coverage of 7600\u201310\u2009600\u2009\u00c5 over most of the field of view, with a spectral resolution <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2248\u00a02800\u20133300, sampled at 0.74\u2009\u00c5\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup> in wavelength.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For J1436+4943, we acquired six exposures totalling 2943\u2009sec integration, with sub-pixel dithers to improve sampling in the across-slice dimension. The seeing was \u223c0.75\u2009arcsec FWHM, estimated from focus-sequence images of a star taken close to the observation time. For J1701+3722, a single 900\u2009sec exposure was obtained, and the seeing was \u223c0.5\u2009arcsec; hence, the PSF in this observation is severely undersampled by the 0.44\u2009arcsec slices.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The data were reduced using the observatory pipeline software. The wavelength calibration solution was obtained from the science frames themselves, using the numerous night-sky emission lines as a simultaneous reference source. No flux calibration has been performed.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156932 id=\"192156932\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 SDSS\u2009J143607.49+494313.2</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The J1436+4943 system was first identified as a possible multiple-imaging system by Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). The foreground galaxy is an elliptical at redshift <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.125, with a velocity dispersion \u03c3\u00a0=\u00a0282\u00a0\u00b1\u00a010\u2009km\u2009s\u2009<sup>\u22121</sup> from the single-fibre SDSS spectrum (Abazajian et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>). MaNGA revealed background [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] emission at <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.231, apparently forming two separate arcs east and west of the target galaxy (Talbot et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> shows the net [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] emission-line image for the source, from the Subaru data. The lens light has been subtracted using the neighbouring continuum, and a correction has been made to remove a radial trend in the net image (caused by gradients in spectral features in the lens galaxy). The [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] image confirms the presence of an extended arc (labelled A and B) to the east, and a western counter-image (C), suggesting a cusp lens configuration. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet in the spectra for the three labelled regions.</p>                        <a id=\"192156935\" scrollto-destination=\"192156935\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/m_slaa003fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&amp;Signature=j6ObQYy6-HLCwFy-zzmzsXzRO~lDnhWaPMIrVfewy8BCJ1GLVy4MRK8yjOYzzREVZ3MKVozFiwALDMqBJUNvJFLL~2AhxtQRI9MvsxGV7CoVBeG-DS4mfFWNOWTs73MAyEF4r9jzuAX4zSmEY9YvJXQVE9~jZxELMG9Y1CmqhNMAdGf~l7oITscHvvj15E0hTTbJKqSFV62yEqJaKdNd61JrOVFQNc8MRxaDrrmmcEZaq5XIDEPhfhx2nJczG09ePLlJ0pqivHC82bcn7OwtGUoF9BGA6Qrh9zA-zV6jTfQIhsmJ99N6kwws9cIDndo3-Tocn~Q8A070BgarhmbBBg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Net emission-line image for the $z$s\u00a0=\u00a01.231 [O\u2009ii] doublet in the background source of MaNGA lens system J1436+4943. Pixels with increased noise due to sky lines are shown in grey. The flux scale is arbitrary.\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig2.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/192156936/slaa003fig2.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig2.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"192156936\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/slaa003fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&Signature=wRE3yiR7MYHlICxqhDBtoYjJOhnc6FaRc1S3PLA5TrtfvuSpg4983XjpGE4HuYElYlfoK~FvUlvfdWDwrr~WdC2y8nBpNfK5nSPLf~6Ni--VCw2rkUNxO7tVT2XUux6SyZLh0Yf9mh5Z5XUaNfj2ORBalcGOoOHKgiDmj9y6TgKhc8dnamn0Ib5ZBGu-o~CVQlLhB7tPtwdgXmt9OrHXIh1XZV~POY3ddi0gjPG9qI7Htzn6-~GWhsouvin1gYdtOHDJG5cRudf7o7dp8wIvLBITSdfeSm7WTyviyi3t2F2mjECRwDMREMmUTVOo0WnBKThIEMq1JNECUCPis3trpQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=192156936&ar=5698818&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig2.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Extract from the spectrum of the J1436+4943 system showing the <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.231 [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet from the three regions identified in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>. Pixels with increased noise due to sky lines are shown in grey. The flux scale is arbitrary.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">To derive the Einstein radius, we have fitted simple lensing models to the net [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] image using <span class=\"small-caps\">pyautolens</span> (Nightingale et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018a</a>; Nightingale, Dye\u00a0&amp; Massey <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018b</a>). The source galaxy is parametrized with an elliptical S\u00e9rsic profile, while the lens is treated as a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE), with centre, ellipticity, and position angle fixed to those of the lens galaxy light. Fitting for the lens normalization, we obtain \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.02\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u2009arcsec; allowing a free external shear term does not affect the fit. Fitting with a pixelized source, we find \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.08\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04 with no shear, or 2.05\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03 with a free shear term that is fitted to be 3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02\u00a0per\u2009cent. The reconstructed source is compact and unstructured in each case. For the calculations in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>, we adopt \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.03\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04, averaging the results from pixelized and parametric models with shear, with the error reflecting the variation between models.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156938 id=\"192156938\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 SDSS\u2009J170124.01+372258.1</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">J1701+3722 was identified as a multiple-image lens by Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), and also recovered in the Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) search. The foreground galaxy is an elliptical at redshift <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.122, with a velocity dispersion \u03c3\u00a0=\u00a0258\u00a0\u00b1\u00a08\u2009km\u2009s\u2009<sup>\u22121</sup> from the single-fibre SDSS spectrum. MaNGA detected the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>], and H\u2009\u03b2 emission lines from a background source at <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.791.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As discussed by Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), the MaNGA data for J1701+3722 posed two puzzles. First, although the system exhibited a near-complete Einstein ring in the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] and H\u2009\u03b2 lines, only a single south-eastern \u2018arc\u2019 was visible in [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]. Secondly, the estimated Einstein radius of \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.3\u2009arcsec derived from the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] ring was substantially larger than the \u223c1.5\u2009arcsec predicted for an isothermal profile matching the stellar velocity dispersion.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> (left) shows the net emission-line image for the background [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] 5007\u2009\u00c5 line. The south-eastern arc identified from MaNGA is resolved by FOCAS into two distinct sections, labelled A and B, at \u223c1.8\u2009arcsec from the lens centre. Additionally, a probable faint counter-image, C, is now visible at smaller radius, \u223c1.1\u2009arcsec. Turning to the H\u2009\u03b2 line, Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> (centre) shows that features A, B, and (marginally) C are all detected, but the situation is complicated by an additional arc, D, at a radius \u223c2.4\u2009arcsec, which is very faint in the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] image. This feature clearly corresponds to the northern arc seen in H\u2009\u03b2 and [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] in MaNGA. Note that the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet falls shortwards of our spectral coverage with FOCAS.</p>                        <a id=\"192156942\" scrollto-destination=\"192156942\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/m_slaa003fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&amp;Signature=bXZFt3jzn2HpUMd4Owkc~mG78IeFhu9w7l23FQeEC~iI3xM~qj0sLOyi50dKGTdhVOV6CVD0S17E45JjwBFuFdtkcryz-JCeAbtVJU-nKwxhW3j1kt5YZhQS5YmcoVgmy8SiDMn6j3WOOFMflKgBY0YGnuyvkhtwksGnOFuj9rZbp8IIkQjXYmN7mNDu6e9cDa1wh~jC-ZwBaq4r1aP0y8mxCP0h09n1kPA2M3dre2G8cyX9D~1Cp-ZauBncdsqub~3iaUL6l2HL6buwrv7JNBiIw7FvwZdq4KoQ~8QiIZM1yeGx6883wzVISMzsqagIzaraDkNj46WWSBHoIkYnTA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Net emission-line images for the $z$s\u00a0=\u00a00.791 background source in MaNGA lens system J1701+3722. The dashed red circle indicates the derived Einstein radius \u03b8Ein\u00a0=\u00a01.63\u2009arcsec.\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig3.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/192156942/slaa003fig3.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig3.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"192156942\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/slaa003fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&Signature=fKGBJhGVom5pLPN3jRgGZaY-AVnKfTWMTRQBMO0tr4x~PTzRiRwZGiiTOmQmUmfpTqDyFxk4N3LXK8QDJDbZgBrab71vnHz2za3FkzPVcnK6H~XX4sBbPXELCYTo9Iv6vcJwlo4s3KbRhUQTC9tWHV1UvYVOThC3jaMt--vzZjvguM8FreYkzDG5j~Z6PBGa4tk48BB50l7cHaCJ6JJqf~R3lq~nK5me444aepusLV~GlEFcKp8er81uAeiuRC8YZQqVn80aT1BsP1n4wxD2ZNHBF9VXjW-1Lhn5eYN9wfcR1eqwahhY6xqUGl~Xs6etnYQIqHblqNWtGRtqJ8b2fg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=192156942&ar=5698818&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig3.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Net emission-line images for the <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.791 background source in MaNGA lens system J1701+3722. Orientation and scale are as in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>. The left-hand and central panels are centred on [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and H\u2009\u03b2 for the source that forms images A, B, and C. The right-hand panel is offset to shorter wavelength, isolating the H\u2009\u03b2-bright contaminating source, D. Coloured crosses mark the centres of regions used to extract the spectra in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>. The dashed red circle indicates the derived Einstein radius \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.63\u2009arcsec.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> shows spectra from the regions discussed. The spectrum of the putative counter-image C is indistinguishable from those of A and B (similar line ratios and &lt;20\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup> velocity difference), supporting the origin of all three in a single source. The spectrum of arc D, however, not only exhibits the very different [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]-to-H\u2009\u03b2 ratio already seen in the images, but is also offset to lower velocity, by 60\u00a0\u00b1\u00a010\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Clearly, D does not originate from the same part of the source plane as A, B, and C; it is presumably a neighbouring galaxy (at separation \u223c7\u2009kpc, for the lens model derived below). In Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> (right), we exploit the velocity offset by selecting a slightly bluer and narrower wavelength interval, to isolate arc D. (The image position shifts, indicating a velocity gradient along this arc.) Given the Einstein radius of the lens derived in the following section, we should expect a counter-image to D, at a radius of \u223c0.7\u2009arcsec, but we cannot confidently identify such a feature in the present data.</p>                        <a id=\"192156944\" scrollto-destination=\"192156944\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/m_slaa003fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&amp;Signature=tPGmZ3LyiP0HGbD70GyAIciDHgdNU332NbCv7w8hrmUSDDHE4nxK9DG4bU7wOP1r2Tr0UHATaEv~jgY9Wzq-4WZymXEshGYPiTWOWA3XoVA5Enw1vcFuZdEFbjROXOpUJQiBxCSrb~BoCB8mTyEAUioR8Rd1tn4RGUanluxgPiGs2CGpBbjPJQ9A-Qq5XIh3QT2XdqicO~TeISbUuKYRJS3Df44mkHmA~0TcQJA1l5huCz-XY~~aZPr9aiTzwaJqOj9V0lTNQjsdSmoPcxp7FSu2hp9B8lAEL9lL88XhL7SYQi7ihXInzJXWtdSadLmNc-UDIodqt6S-6MF1ZCku1Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Extracts from the spectrum of the J1701+3722 system showing the $z$s\u00a0=\u00a00.791 [O\u2009iii] and H\u2009\u03b2 lines from the four arcs as identified in Fig.\u00a03. Regions of increased noise are shown in grey. Note the small velocity offset (\u223c60\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>) and very different line ratios in the spectrum of arc D.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/m_slaa003fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&amp;Signature=tPGmZ3LyiP0HGbD70GyAIciDHgdNU332NbCv7w8hrmUSDDHE4nxK9DG4bU7wOP1r2Tr0UHATaEv~jgY9Wzq-4WZymXEshGYPiTWOWA3XoVA5Enw1vcFuZdEFbjROXOpUJQiBxCSrb~BoCB8mTyEAUioR8Rd1tn4RGUanluxgPiGs2CGpBbjPJQ9A-Qq5XIh3QT2XdqicO~TeISbUuKYRJS3Df44mkHmA~0TcQJA1l5huCz-XY~~aZPr9aiTzwaJqOj9V0lTNQjsdSmoPcxp7FSu2hp9B8lAEL9lL88XhL7SYQi7ihXInzJXWtdSadLmNc-UDIodqt6S-6MF1ZCku1Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Extracts from the spectrum of the J1701+3722 system showing the $z$s\u00a0=\u00a00.791 [O\u2009iii] and H\u2009\u03b2 lines from the four arcs as identified in Fig.\u00a03. Regions of increased noise are shown in grey. Note the small velocity offset (\u223c60\u2009km\u2009s\u22121) and very different line ratios in the spectrum of arc D.\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig4.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/192156944/slaa003fig4.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig4.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"192156944\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/slaa003fig4.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&Signature=KlvTpgqpcGsH2zfFbdDsWNStH0XL3ew3gB-mD8yXhJzB-OgJuhuc0Kfo65YcYL3Dp-j6qA87wwylCKxHeFx3MP3-1vDjBI~qQD2lYl8FPTZmbaJabjLd-siZw7-ZDfnWrB1sGdBjcTq6OTNEGcPQAlQl9SBiMRy0nIlTaNcy7fqC0xYx~MkoXYrT-MA4fKnW~VEUnSdMR~S0gi73lXXRMRLwcFU-zr9Y5Qu7~eFOsz0CGob3Kq1QXPfEcJJck7~pIPaeKYeQMUur-t2MjstrP5LsHAlps4xJ0qfPJk7DxdLqbr9KAWk5k~33P8pXfW82iObvVlSa-5kgJy1i6cO4yA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=192156944&ar=5698818&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig4.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Extracts from the spectrum of the J1701+3722 system showing the <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.791 [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and H\u2009\u03b2 lines from the four arcs as identified in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>. Regions of increased noise are shown in grey. Note the small velocity offset (\u223c60\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>) and very different line ratios in the spectrum of arc D.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Even after excluding the contaminating H\u2009\u03b2 source, it is difficult to fit our data for J1701+3722 using pixelized lensing models. Specifically, we find that the optimization always favours slightly improving the fit to arcs A and B, at the expense of not producing any counter-image at C. This is not a failing of the modelling method, but reflects the limitations of our data for this system, e.g. undersampled PSF and strongly correlated pixels (after rebinning on to square pixels), due to the lack of dithered pointings.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We proceed on the assumption that C is genuinely a counter-image to A and B, and crudely enforce this \u2018qualitative\u2019 aspect of the model by artificially reducing the noise map values around C, to assign it greater weight. With this approach, we obtain acceptable fits to an SIE with geometry (centre, axial ratio, and position angle) fixed to the lens light, and a sizeable shear of amplitude \u223c12\u00a0per\u2009cent (representing angular structure in the mass not captured in the SIE, and/or external perturbations). For a pixelized source, we obtain \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.62\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u2009arcsec. Fitting with a parametrized Sersic source yields \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.64\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01\u2009arcsec. We adopt the average of these values in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>. However, to reflect the greater systematic uncertainty in modelling J1701+3722, we impose a 10\u00a0per\u2009cent error on \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>; deeper and (especially) cleaner data are still required for this lens.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156947 id=\"192156947\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 MASS-TO-LIGHT RATIOS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we derive estimates of the total mass-to-light ratio within the Einstein radius, (<em>M</em>/<em>L</em>)<sub>Ein</sub>, for each lens, and (with assumptions for the dark-matter contribution and the galaxy age) the stellar mass-to-light ratio, <em>\u03a5</em>, and the IMF mass-excess factor, \u03b1.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The first part of Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> details the observed parameters used in the calculations, i.e. the lens and source redshifts, the Einstein radius, and the Einstein-aperture magnitudes in the <em>i</em> band, as measured from the SDSS imaging. For reference, we also note the effective radius and velocity dispersion. We have applied corrections of \u223c0.1\u2009mag for the \u223c1\u2009arcsec SDSS PSF, derived from fits with <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). The second part of the table reports the projected Einstein radius in kpc, and the corresponding projected mass (<em>M</em><sub>Ein</sub>) and luminosity (<em>L</em><sub>Ein</sub>). The luminosities assume galactic extinction corrections of \u223c0.04\u2009mag in <em>i</em> from Schlafly\u00a0&amp; Finkbeiner (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>), a band-shifting correction of \u223c0.09\u2009mag derived using <span class=\"small-caps\">ezgal</span> (Mancone\u00a0&amp; Gonzalez <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), and a solar absolute magnitude of <em>M</em><sub>\u2299, <em>i</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a04.53 from the same source.</p>                        <a id=\"192156950\" scrollto-destination=\"192156950\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Adopted parameters and derived quantities from the mass-to-light ratio calculations. The aperture magnitude is quoted before and after correction for the PSF. Luminosities and mass-to-light ratios all refer to the rest-frame SDSS <em>i</em> band and include correction for band-shifting and galactic extinction. <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub> is the expected stellar mass-to-light ratio for a Kroupa IMF, given our assumptions for age and metallicity.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>Quantity<span aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/192156950\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">In the third part of Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>, we compute the total lensing mass-to-light ratio in the Einstein aperture, which includes contributions from dark matter (and, in principle, from a central black hole, gas, etc., but these are expected to be negligible). To compare this with the value expected from the stars alone, <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>, we used <span class=\"small-caps\">ezgal</span> to derive the latter for stellar population models from Conroy, Gunn\u00a0&amp; White (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>), for metallicities (1.0\u20131.5)\u00d7 the solar value and ages 8\u201312\u2009Gyr (corresponding to formation redshift <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>f</sub>\u00a0&gt;\u00a01.5). The full range in <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub> spanned by these models is 2.41\u20133.46; our calculations adopt this as the 2\u03c3 interval, i.e. we assume <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.93\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.26. These assumptions are supported by fits of single-burst models from Conroy\u00a0&amp; van Dokkum (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) to the Einstein-aperture spectra from MaNGA, which favour ages 9\u201310\u2009Gyr for both galaxies (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>). If all of the lensing mass is attributed to stars, the derived <em>maximum</em> IMF mass factor, \u03b1<sub>max</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0<em>M</em>/(<em>L</em><em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>), is intermediate between the values of \u03b1\u00a0=\u00a01.0 for a Kroupa IMF and \u03b1\u00a0\u2248\u00a01.65 for an unbroken power-law IMF with the Salpeter (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1955</a>) slope.</p>                        <a id=\"192156952\" scrollto-destination=\"192156952\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/m_slaa003fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&amp;Signature=gytzDEgfxJbaYSmtXYrUN9LpvrO9fjGyBjlSXmltkABX-Gt4vzn6haq-V2n8kCMrDqOqAF~I6LPPP0k4HW4F3R-HM7Q5S13SQRijyFf~Vx6hMjAIT2lKVsE4O~g1ZKW7esZtOevV~uD9UaelDb0Kl2oQljaecEhkCzRdlTGsAA31BhOuqRdwhlYmlE2CXPR79ttQZS~janyp9d36BLH1C72xhYkRqAKrTUpC1zL~ADl9UyLut-Cd6Qm2zJaY9C87F86J15jJYyvlWhz2sERP9uj5W3DOUQqI0m1FIFwHrLy3ZvtI9fSohYX9Ki3qsddfBpBW1VGzzVmpVFaUPAzKow__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Einstein-aperture spectra for the lens galaxies extracted from the MaNGA data cubes, showing the blue spectral range that is most sensitive to the stellar population age. The fits shown in black were derived from full-spectral fitting to the Conroy\u00a0&amp; van Dokkum (2012) simple stellar population models. The legend indicates the fitted ages, and the element abundances [Mg/H], [Fe/H], [C/H], and [N/H]. The fit residuals are shown beneath. Note that the spectral fits support old ages for both galaxies. The fits shown in black were derived from full-spectral fitting to the Conroy\u00a0&amp; van Dokkum (2012) simple stellar population models. The legend indicates the fitted ages, and the element abundances [Mg/H], [Fe/H], [C/H], and [N/H]. The fit residuals are shown beneath. Note that the spectral fits support old ages for both galaxies. The vertical lines highlight the age-sensitive H\u2009\u03b4, H\u2009\u03b3, and H\u2009\u03b2 lines.\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/192156952/slaa003fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"192156952\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/slaa003fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&Signature=nu18aAoGKgidITUZv3JpLr75EH7439pp1ovW-wV1K4U1pytlNZ~Ymcyd6Y2vlsjKxwuwWx7bY5WiBBsSVfDK8tdbKx98CYFwguRrFVc3xS~~Ei~KPwkPDwdMTpU1q0SUYamJa335XzK-QEK2JQ02fEn85nk9PpZI-wZvDkSpiFbUidbNxxIbfeaoj7P3KdVol7fnC0JzNCRXL11Q1-cM93At~za1vZFn6FRYPzs1At173JTlkUMOAOruLcrLLNTFCUOHD6a1hPgD609WCTjjfeOfG2rkm25Etqp3iutnReoORK2vy2Gz4wzTj8rZxW4cZBjiyKwick36Dgh5DeYflg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=192156952&ar=5698818&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Einstein-aperture spectra for the lens galaxies extracted from the MaNGA data cubes, showing the blue spectral range that is most sensitive to the stellar population age. The fits shown in black were derived from full-spectral fitting to the Conroy\u00a0&amp; van Dokkum (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) simple stellar population models. The legend indicates the fitted ages, and the element abundances [Mg/H], [Fe/H], [C/H], and [N/H]. The fit residuals are shown beneath. Note that the spectral fits support old ages for both galaxies. The vertical lines highlight the age-sensitive H\u2009\u03b4, H\u2009\u03b3, and H\u2009\u03b2 lines.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The final part of Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> records the correction for dark matter, and its effect on the derived stellar mass-to-light ratio, <em>\u03a5</em>. The corrections are based on the scheme described in Smith et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), which uses the projected dark-matter profiles in the EAGLE cosmological simulation, for haloes hosting galaxies with \u03c3\u00a0\u2273\u00a0250\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup> (Schaller et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). The estimated contributions are 35\u00a0\u00b1\u00a06\u00a0per\u2009cent of <em>M</em><sub>Ein</sub> for the MaNGA systems, roughly twice the fraction obtained for the much closer Smith et\u00a0al. lenses. (The error here derives from the scatter among haloes in the simulation.) After subtracting the halo contribution, we arrive at values for the stellar mass-to-light ratio <em>\u03a5</em> and the IMF mass-excess factor \u03b1\u00a0=\u00a0(<em>M</em> \u2212 <em>M</em><sub>DM</sub>)/(<em>L</em><em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>)\u00a0=\u00a0<em>\u03a5</em>/<em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>. For J1436+4943, the resulting \u03b1 is consistent with unity, i.e. the lensing mass is compatible with a Kroupa IMF and the dark matter expected from EAGLE. For J1701+3722, the derived result is lighter than the Kroupa IMF prediction. Heavier-than-Salpeter IMFs are excluded at the &gt;4\u03c3 level.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Our estimates are subject to the usual systematic uncertainties affecting this method. For example, using Maraston (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>) models for <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub> would increase \u03b1 by \u223c12\u00a0per\u2009cent; adopting the Bennett et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) cosmological parameters would increase \u03b1 by 3.5\u00a0per\u2009cent. The recovered \u03b1 anticorrelates with the adopted stellar population age; however, consistency with a Salpeter IMF (\u03b1\u00a0\u2273\u00a01.6) would require ages 4\u20135\u2009Gyr, which are excluded by the weakness of the H\u2009\u03b3 and H\u2009\u03b4 absorption lines.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Although the IMF constraints for the two galaxies studied here are similar to those obtained from lower redshift lenses (Newman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Collier et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), we stress that the current results apply at larger radius (3.7\u20134.7\u2009kpc, compared to \u223c2\u2009kpc), and are more dependent on the accuracy of the dark-matter correction.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156956 id=\"192156956\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>6 SUMMARY</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have presented Subaru observations of two <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.12 strong lenses originally identified from the SDSS-IV MaNGA survey. For each of these systems, the increased signal-to-noise and resolution greatly improve on the previous data. We have definitively established J1436+4943 as a multiple-image lens, with a secure Einstein radius. For J1701+3722, we have confirmed that two background sources are present, as suspected from MaNGA, and removed the contamination from the second source to derive a new lensing model that is more consistent with the velocity dispersion.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">After correction for the dark-matter contributions expected from cosmological simulations, the lensing-derived stellar mass-to-light ratios for the two galaxies are consistent with (or even lighter than) a Kroupa (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>) IMF like that in the Milky Way. At face value, this <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span> =\u00a00.12 application of \u2018pure lensing\u2019 (without dynamical information) supports the \u2018lightweight\u2019 IMFs derived from lenses at <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span>\u00a0=\u00a00.03\u20130.07 (Newman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Collier et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), albeit at a larger physical radius, and with a greater reliance on the correctness of our estimated dark-matter contributions.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The observations described here demonstrate the suitability of the FOCAS IFU for galaxy-scale lensing science. The MaNGA systems were observed as validation targets during a Subaru search for low-redshift strong-lensing ellipticals; the results of the search programme will be presented in a future paper.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156960 id=\"192156960\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" data-legacy-id=ack1>ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">RJS and JRL were supported by the Science and Technology Facilities Council through the Durham Astronomy Consolidated Grant 2017\u20132020 (ST/P000541/1); RJS also acknowledges travel funding from PATT Linked Grant 2019\u20132020 (ST/S001557/1). <div class=\"fpage\">819</div> <div class=\"pub-id\"><a href=\"https://doi.org/10.1093/pasj/54.6.819\" class=\"link link-doi openInAnotherWindow\" class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://dx.doi.org/10.1093/pasj/54.6.819\" target=\"_blank\">Crossref</a></div><div class=\"adsDoiReference hide\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" a central black hole, gas, etc., but these are expected to be negligible). To compare this with the value expected from the stars alone, <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>, we used <span class=\"small-caps\">ezgal</span> to derive the latter for stellar population models from Conroy, Gunn\u00a0&amp; White (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>), for metallicities (1.0\u20131.5)\u00d7 the solar value and ages 8\u201312\u2009Gyr (corresponding to formation redshift <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>f</sub>\u00a0&gt;\u00a01.5). The full range in <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub> spanned by these models is 2.41\u20133.46; our calculations adopt this as the 2\u03c3 interval, i.e. we assume <em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.93\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.26. These assumptions are supported by fits of single-burst models from Conroy\u00a0&amp; van Dokkum (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) to the Einstein-aperture spectra from MaNGA, which favour ages 9\u201310\u2009Gyr for both galaxies (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>). If all of the lensing mass is attributed to stars, the derived <em>maximum</em> IMF mass factor, \u03b1<sub>max</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0<em>M</em>/(<em>L</em><em>\u03a5</em><sub>ref</sub>), is intermediate between the values of \u03b1\u00a0=\u00a01.0 for a Kroupa IMF and \u03b1\u00a0\u2248\u00a01.65 for an unbroken power-law IMF with the Salpeter (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156920 id=\"192156920\" class=\"abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present new observations of two <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span>\u00a0=\u00a00.12 strong-lensing elliptical galaxies, originally discovered from the SDSS-IV MaNGA survey, using the new FOCAS IFU spectrograph on the Subaru Telescope. For J1436+4943, our observations confirm the identification of this system as a multiple-image lens, in a cusp configuration, with an Einstein radius \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.0\u2009arcsec. For J1701+3722, the improved data confirm earlier hints of a complex source plane, with different configurations evident in different emission lines. The new observations reveal a previously unseen inner counter-image to the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] arc found from MaNGA, leading to a smaller revised Einstein radius of \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.6\u2009arcsec. The inferred projected masses within the Einstein apertures (3.7\u20134.7\u2009kpc) are consistent with being dominated by stars with an initial mass function (IMF) similar to that of the Milky Way, and a dark matter contribution of \u223c35\u00a0per\u2009cent as supported from cosmological simulations. These results are consistent with \u2018pure lensing\u2019 analyses of lower redshift lenses, but contrast with claims for heavier IMFs from combined lensing and dynamical studies of more distant early-type galaxies.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD&quot;\">galaxies: elliptical and lenticular, cD</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156922 id=\"192156922\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Strong gravitational lensing is a key tool for measuring extragalactic masses and probing the distribution of dark and luminous matter in galaxies (e.g. Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). Analysing a sample of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00.2 strong-lensing elliptical galaxies, Treu et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) found that their velocity dispersions and projected lensing masses could only be reconciled with a universal dark matter profile if the stellar mass-to-light ratio, <em>\u03a5</em>, was larger than expected for an initial mass function (IMF) like that in the Milky Way (e.g. Kroupa <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). By contrast, for the few known nearby (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$z$|</span>\u00a0=\u00a00.03\u20130.07) strong lenses, lensing <em>alone</em> constrains <em>\u03a5</em> to be close to the value expected from the Kroupa IMF (Collier, Smith\u00a0&amp; Lucey <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). In these low-redshift systems, the arcs are formed at smaller physical radius, minimizing the contributions from dark matter, which obviates the need for dynamical information to separate dark and stellar components. One possible resolution of the tension between the above results, discussed by Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), is that steep inner gradients in <em>\u03a5</em> may inflate the central velocity dispersion, causing the combined lensing and dynamics analysis to assign too much mass to the stellar component and too little to the dark halo.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Establishing well-constrained lenses at intermediate distances should help to solve the apparent discrepancy between the nearby and distant samples. Smith, Lucey\u00a0&amp; Conroy (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) presented the first use of integral field unit (IFU) spectroscopy as a tool to discover lensed line-emitting sources behind bright foreground galaxies. This method, applied to individually targeted lens candidates, has also been adapted to the VLT MUSE spectrograph (Smith et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Collier et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1_68_1579329418409\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1_68_1579329418409\" data-open=\"bib1_68_1579329418409\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>). A complementary approach is to exploit data from large multi-IFU surveys. The SDSS-IV MaNGA survey (Bundy et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) is acquiring IFU observations for thousands of nearby galaxies, including hundreds of massive ellipticals, which are the most effective gravitational lenses.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Two groups have searched the MaNGA data cubes for lens systems. Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) (and unpublished extensions) conducted a semi-automated search in the MaNGA data releases DR13\u2013DR15, restricted to \u223c600 galaxies with a velocity dispersion \u03c3\u00a0&gt;\u00a0200\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>, which dominate the total strong-lensing cross-section. Independently, Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) searched all targets in DR13\u2013DR14 using a more automated source detection method, though retaining a manual inspection step. Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) reported the discovery of a lensed source behind J1701+3722, apparently showing a near-complete Einstein ring in [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], but only a single \u2018arc\u2019 in [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]. He estimated an Einstein radius of 2.3\u2009arcsec, but noted that this is uncomfortably large compared to the measured velocity dispersion. The Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) search yielded seven new apparent multiple-imaging systems as well as confirming the identification of J1701+3722. In a subsequent reanalysis of the data, we could not convincingly reproduce many of these systems (see discussion in Smith, Lucey\u00a0&amp; Collier <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), but J1436+4943, which was missed in Smith\u2019s visual search, is a compelling candidate for further study.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this letter, we present follow-up observations of J1436+4943 and J1701+3722, obtained with the new IFU mode of the FOCAS spectrograph at the Subaru telescope (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>). The new observations have much higher spatial resolution than the MaNGA discovery data, and also higher spectral resolution, enabling a more detailed reanalysis of the two lenses (Sections\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>). Combining the measured Einstein radii with photometry and estimates for the dark matter contributions and likely stellar ages, we derive results on the total and stellar mass-to-light ratios, and constraints on the IMF through the mass-excess factor (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>). The work is briefly summarized in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We adopt the cosmological parameters from Planck Collaboration VI (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156928 id=\"192156928\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 SUBARU FOCAS IFU OBSERVATIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We observed J1436+4943 and J1701+3722 using the Subaru FOCAS IFU during its first night of scientific operations, on 2019 June 26. The design and characteristics of the IFU are fully described by Ozaki et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, and in preparation). Briefly, the unit is an image slicer that reformats a 10.1\u00a0\u00d7\u00a013.5\u2009arcsec<sup>2</sup> field of view into 23 slices of width 0.44\u2009arcsec, sampled with 0.2\u2009arcsec pixels; the IFU feeds the existing FOCAS spectrograph (Kashikawa et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). We observed with the VPH900 grism, providing a wavelength coverage of 7600\u201310\u2009600\u2009\u00c5 over most of the field of view, with a spectral resolution <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2248\u00a02800\u20133300, sampled at 0.74\u2009\u00c5\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup> in wavelength.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">For J1436+4943, we acquired six exposures totalling 2943\u2009sec integration, with sub-pixel dithers to improve sampling in the across-slice dimension. The seeing was \u223c0.75\u2009arcsec FWHM, estimated from focus-sequence images of a star taken close to the observation time. For J1701+3722, a single 900\u2009sec exposure was obtained, and the seeing was \u223c0.5\u2009arcsec; hence, the PSF in this observation is severely undersampled by the 0.44\u2009arcsec slices.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The data were reduced using the observatory pipeline software. The wavelength calibration solution was obtained from the science frames themselves, using the numerous night-sky emission lines as a simultaneous reference source. No flux calibration has been performed.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156932 id=\"192156932\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 SDSS\u2009J143607.49+494313.2</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The J1436+4943 system was first identified as a possible multiple-imaging system by Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). The foreground galaxy is an elliptical at redshift <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.125, with a velocity dispersion \u03c3\u00a0=\u00a0282\u00a0\u00b1\u00a010\u2009km\u2009s\u2009<sup>\u22121</sup> from the single-fibre SDSS spectrum (Abazajian et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>). MaNGA revealed background [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] emission at <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.231, apparently forming two separate arcs east and west of the target galaxy (Talbot et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> shows the net [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] emission-line image for the source, from the Subaru data. The lens light has been subtracted using the neighbouring continuum, and a correction has been made to remove a radial trend in the net image (caused by gradients in spectral features in the lens galaxy). The [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] image confirms the presence of an extended arc (labelled A and B) to the east, and a western counter-image (C), suggesting a cusp lens configuration. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet in the spectra for the three labelled regions.</p>                        <a id=\"192156935\" scrollto-destination=\"192156935\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/m_slaa003fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&amp;Signature=j6ObQYy6-HLCwFy-zzmzsXzRO~lDnhWaPMIrVfewy8BCJ1GLVy4MRK8yjOYzzREVZ3MKVozFiwALDMqBJUNvJFLL~2AhxtQRI9MvsxGV7CoVBeG-DS4mfFWNOWTs73MAyEF4r9jzuAX4zSmEY9YvJXQVE9~jZxELMG9Y1CmqhNMAdGf~l7oITscHvvj15E0hTTbJKqSFV62yEqJaKdNd61JrOVFQNc8MRxaDrrmmcEZaq5XIDEPhfhx2nJczG09ePLlJ0pqivHC82bcn7OwtGUoF9BGA6Qrh9zA-zV6jTfQIhsmJ99N6kwws9cIDndo3-Tocn~Q8A070BgarhmbBBg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Net emission-line image for the $z$s\u00a0=\u00a01.231 [O\u2009ii] doublet in the background source of MaNGA lens system J1436+4943. North is at the top, east at the left, and axis ticks are spaced by 1 arcsec. Coloured crosses mark the centres of regions used to extract the spectra in Fig.\u00a02. The dashed red circle indicates the derived Einstein radius \u03b8Ein\u00a0=\u00a02.03\u2009arcsec.\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig1.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/192156935/slaa003fig1.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig1.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"192156935\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/slaa003fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&Signature=034l675l5eWImva2PrjOVJmn8gqjlWto0xQ62ilhYeewG41QYWm2t27hiyZSixYcWBrtBxkf5j6vdEQyZVNSmMiZ6Sotm1l00u4U8pDDqha1ZJzZ68qcnyqRSMWWjAPB8QH8dfFmxPPINjal5c0VWgLahjv8qoDZ9z0ai36BE8qGk-EbfZKE9LRqq44SzCklvOvIziPOHEqfiUd2s02lNuTiklEptjKVxPnR8YI5t5ZLRmXyseGcAR6-D-YvDZFSd92k9avTjBEDK7f~-8sHqZ417MraQ1dw3vUxzOUpNvVOaF2mmF3hscN8M2ktxqwg~h9XG792NrnR2tSF371o6Q__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=192156935&ar=5698818&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig1.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Net emission-line image for the <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.231 [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet in the background source of MaNGA lens system J1436+4943. North is at the top, east at the left, and axis ticks are spaced by 1 arcsec. Coloured crosses mark the centres of regions used to extract the spectra in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. Pixels with increased noise due to sky lines are shown in grey. The flux scale is arbitrary.\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig2.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/192156936/slaa003fig2.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig2.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"192156936\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/slaa003fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&Signature=wRE3yiR7MYHlICxqhDBtoYjJOhnc6FaRc1S3PLA5TrtfvuSpg4983XjpGE4HuYElYlfoK~FvUlvfdWDwrr~WdC2y8nBpNfK5nSPLf~6Ni--VCw2rkUNxO7tVT2XUux6SyZLh0Yf9mh5Z5XUaNfj2ORBalcGOoOHKgiDmj9y6TgKhc8dnamn0Ib5ZBGu-o~CVQlLhB7tPtwdgXmt9OrHXIh1XZV~POY3ddi0gjPG9qI7Htzn6-~GWhsouvin1gYdtOHDJG5cRudf7o7dp8wIvLBITSdfeSm7WTyviyi3t2F2mjECRwDMREMmUTVOo0WnBKThIEMq1JNECUCPis3trpQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=192156936&ar=5698818&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5327\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"slaa003fig2.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Extract from the spectrum of the J1436+4943 system showing the <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.231 [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet from the three regions identified in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>. Pixels with increased noise due to sky lines are shown in grey. The flux scale is arbitrary.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">To derive the Einstein radius, we have fitted simple lensing models to the net [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] image using <span class=\"small-caps\">pyautolens</span> (Nightingale et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018a</a>; Nightingale, Dye\u00a0&amp; Massey <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018b</a>). The source galaxy is parametrized with an elliptical S\u00e9rsic profile, while the lens is treated as a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE), with centre, ellipticity, and position angle fixed to those of the lens galaxy light. Fitting for the lens normalization, we obtain \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.02\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u2009arcsec; allowing a free external shear term does not affect the fit. Fitting with a pixelized source, we find \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.08\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04 with no shear, or 2.05\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03 with a free shear term that is fitted to be 3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02\u00a0per\u2009cent. The reconstructed source is compact and unstructured in each case. For the calculations in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>, we adopt \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.03\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04, averaging the results from pixelized and parametric models with shear, with the error reflecting the variation between models.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=192156938 id=\"192156938\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 SDSS\u2009J170124.01+372258.1</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">J1701+3722 was identified as a multiple-image lens by Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), and also recovered in the Talbot et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) search. The foreground galaxy is an elliptical at redshift <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>l</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.122, with a velocity dispersion \u03c3\u00a0=\u00a0258\u00a0\u00b1\u00a08\u2009km\u2009s\u2009<sup>\u22121</sup> from the single-fibre SDSS spectrum. MaNGA detected the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>], and H\u2009\u03b2 emission lines from a background source at <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z$|</span><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.791.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As discussed by Smith (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), the MaNGA data for J1701+3722 posed two puzzles. First, although the system exhibited a near-complete Einstein ring in the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] and H\u2009\u03b2 lines, only a single south-eastern \u2018arc\u2019 was visible in [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]. Secondly, the estimated Einstein radius of \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0=\u00a02.3\u2009arcsec derived from the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] ring was substantially larger than the \u223c1.5\u2009arcsec predicted for an isothermal profile matching the stellar velocity dispersion.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> (left) shows the net emission-line image for the background [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] 5007\u2009\u00c5 line. The south-eastern arc identified from MaNGA is resolved by FOCAS into two distinct sections, labelled A and B, at \u223c1.8\u2009arcsec from the lens centre. Additionally, a probable faint counter-image, C, is now visible at smaller radius, \u223c1.1\u2009arcsec. Turning to the H\u2009\u03b2 line, Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> (centre) shows that features A, B, and (marginally) C are all detected, but the situation is complicated by an additional arc, D, at a radius \u223c2.4\u2009arcsec, which is very faint in the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] image. This feature clearly corresponds to the northern arc seen in H\u2009\u03b2 and [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] in MaNGA. Note that the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet falls shortwards of our spectral coverage with FOCAS.</p>                        <a id=\"192156942\" scrollto-destination=\"192156942\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnrasl/493/1/10.1093_mnrasl_slaa003/2/m_slaa003fig3.jpeg?Expires=1611464421&amp;Signature=bXZFt3jzn2HpUMd4Owkc~mG78IeFhu9w7l23FQeEC~iI3xM~qj0sLOyi50dKGTdhVOV6CVD0S17E45JjwBFuFdtkcryz-JCeAbtVJU-nKwxhW3j1kt5YZhQS5YmcoVgmy8SiDMn6j3WOOFMflKgBY0YGnuyvkhtwksGnOFuj9rZbp8IIkQjXYmN7mNDu6e9cDa1wh~jC-ZwBaq4r1aP0y8mxCP0h09n1kPA2M3dre2G8cyX9D~1Cp-ZauBncdsqub~3iaUL6l2HL6buwrv7JNBiIw7FvwZdq4KoQ~8QiIZM1yeGx6883wzVISMzsqagIzaraDkNj46WWSBHoIkYnTA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Net emission-line images for the $z$s\u00a0=\u00a00.791 background source in MaNGA lens system J1701+3722.
